  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8b74c026-d3b4-4524-a254-ff30b7fd0acd'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer12811414273465398721">The past few years have held more surprises than part-angel Clara Gardner could ever have anticipated. Yet from the dizzying highs of first love, to the agonizing low of losing someone close to her, the one thing she can no longer deny is that she was never meant to live a normal life.<br/> <br/>Since discovering the special role she plays among the other angel-bloods, Clara has bee</span>
  <span id="freeText12811414273465398721" style="display:none">The past few years have held more surprises than part-angel Clara Gardner could ever have anticipated. Yet from the dizzying highs of first love, to the agonizing low of losing someone close to her, the one thing she can no longer deny is that she was never meant to live a normal life.<br /> <br />Since discovering the special role she plays among the other angel-bloods, Clara has been determined to protect Tucker Avery from the evil that follows her . . . even if it means breaking both their hearts. Leaving town seems like the best option, so she’s headed back to California - and so is Christian Prescott, the irresistible boy from the vision that started her on this journey in the first place.<br /> <br />As Clara makes her way in a world that is frighteningly new, she discovers that the fallen angel who attacked her is watching her every move. And he’s not the only one. . . . With the battle against the Black Wings looming, Clara knows she must finally fulfill her destiny. But it won’t come without sacrifices and betrayal.<br /> <br />In the riveting finale of the Unearthly series, Clara must decide her fate once and for all.</span>

    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235289321?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2013-publication">2013-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=crush-worthy-boys">crush-worthy-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235289321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer658242661916031672">Our Boundless <a href='http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/01/boundless-tour-stop-cynthia-hand.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Interview & ARC Giveaway with Cynthia Hand</a> is up!<br/><br/><b>This review is spoiler-free</b>, and safe even if you haven't read the first two books in the series. (But if you haven't--sheesh, what are you waiting for?!)<br/><br/>After waiting for <i>Boundless</i> for so long, I was strangely nervous about reading it. When the package arrived, I literally hugged it for a full minute because I knew what was inside! All day long, I was scared to even peek at the first page, so it wasn't until after midnight that I st</span>
  <span id="freeText658242661916031672" style="display:none">Our Boundless <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/01/boundless-tour-stop-cynthia-hand.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Interview &amp; ARC Giveaway with Cynthia Hand</a> is up!<br /><br /><b>This review is spoiler-free</b>, and safe even if you haven't read the first two books in the series. (But if you haven't--sheesh, what are you waiting for?!)<br /><br />After waiting for <i>Boundless</i> for so long, I was strangely nervous about reading it. When the package arrived, I literally hugged it for a full minute because I knew what was inside! All day long, I was scared to even peek at the first page, so it wasn't until after midnight that I started the book. But my burning need to know how this incredible story ended kept me up through the night until I finally finished it at 4 in the morning.<br /><br />This final installment in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> series picks up shortly after the novella <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15851966.Radiant__Unearthly___2_5_" title="Radiant (Unearthly, #2.5) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Radiant</a>, as Clara begins her freshman year at Stanford University. She's trying to balance a normal life with her divine purpose as an Angelblood, even as her dreams are plagued by disturbing visions. Clara still feels the absence of those she loves, even though Angela and Christian are both there at school with her--and though her relationship with Tucker changed after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a>, she just can't stop thinking about him. Every decision Clara makes now has an impact on her future, as well as the safety--and happiness--of those around her.<br /><br />As always with this series, <i>Boundless</i> is beautifully written, and filled with humor, depth, and emotion. <b>My favorite moments include:</b> a walk among the redwoods; Clara learning to impart her glory to help others; training sessions with an important tutor; unexpectedly poignant interactions with the still-scary Samjeeza; the freedom and joy of flying; an arresting, despairing vision of hell; a slow-burning buildup to an exciting climax; and above all, a gorgeous moment high on a rock with someone she holds dear. I've also rarely seen parental love depicted in such a warm and loving way, and there are scenes here that clutched at my heart unbearably. I appreciate how full and busy and purposeful Clara's life is; each activity she undertakes and each relationship she maintains is a formative part of her, but none of them define her as a person or as an angel. I wish more young adult novels took such care in showing this balance between life and love in a way that is so organic to the plot.<br /><br />There are, however, some elements that leave me conflicted. For me, it was a little too easy to guess who the traitor was; the pacing in the middle of the book felt a bit uneven and left me at odds with the romantic developments; and I thought Clara's relationships with both Tucker and Christian relied a bit too much on our past history and knowledge of what has come before. I went into this book loving both boys and feeling that no matter what choice Clara makes, I would feel okay with it because I thought it would feel right. And in some ways, that's still true--I think most readers will be satisfied with how this complicated entanglement is resolved. But because there is so much back and forth in this book as Clara is pulled between her feelings, and because I struggle with how fair the conclusion might be to certain parties, I'm not sure that I am quite there yet in celebrating what occurs. Even though things wrap up pretty neatly here, I feel like I still need more closure, so I'm kind of hoping that the author writes a follow-up story one day. I can dream, right?<br /><br />But love is a painful, complex, and ever-evolving thing, and the concerns of mere mortals don't always apply when it comes to angels. Even with separation and danger and loss, there is a great deal of hope and promise for this indelible trio, as well as for Angela, and for Clara's parents. There is so much love in these books in its many different forms, and I feel the glow of it long after I turn the last page.<br /><br /><b>Without a doubt, this is one of the best paranormal romance series ever written.</b> <i>Boundless</i> is a strong and satisfying conclusion to an incredible series that sets a new benchmark for paranormal romance. The passionate discussions about the books speak to the strong emotions that these characters inspire, and I know that I am all the more enriched for having known them. While this particular book is bittersweet, my heart is certainly lifted by the promise of things to come.<br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/01/boundless-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher.</i><br /><br /><b>Don't miss our Q &amp; A with Cynthia Hand on January 25th!</b> We're going to be chatting about Clara's divine purpose, the author's upcoming projects, and obviously fangirling over Tucker and Christian. We'll also be giving away our ARC to one lucky winner! In the meantime, you can also read our epic interview with Cynthia from last year <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2012/01/epic-cynthia-hand-interview-part-one.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> and <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2012/01/epic-cynthia-hand-interview-part-two.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>) if you're interested.<br /><br />Thoughtful discussion is absolutely welcome below, but <b>PLEASE USE SPOILER TAGS</b> where appropriate. It isn't fair to ruin this for people who haven't had a chance to read it yet. </span>
  <a data-text-id="658242661916031672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_236205080" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236205080" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236205080?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Unearthly fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=left-me-in-a-sad-emotional-state">left-me-in-a-sad-emotional-state</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=harpercollins">harpercollins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=oh-yeah-baby">oh-yeah-baby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=awesome">awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=cool-author">cool-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236205080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8523382919340352100">Actual rating: 3.5 stars<br/><br/>It's always a sad day when I must say goodbye to a series that I've come to love over the years. You feel so invested in the characters that you just don't want it to be over. But what's really the nail biter is the concern of the final book ending on a high note. Will it meet your expectations? Will it be just a satisfying conclusion? Will it completely suck? I mean, who wants to remember a series thinking, "Awww, man! This series was great... until the author <em>blew</em> it in</span>
  <span id="freeText8523382919340352100" style="display:none">Actual rating: 3.5 stars<br><br>It's always a sad day when I must say goodbye to a series that I've come to love over the years. You feel so invested in the characters that you just don't want it to be over. But what's really the nail biter is the concern of the final book ending on a high note. Will it meet your expectations? Will it be just a satisfying conclusion? Will it completely suck? I mean, who wants to remember a series thinking, "Awww, man! This series was great... until the author <em>blew</em> it in the final book. Such a shame really." Fortunately, I think <em>Boundless</em> was great for <em>most</em> of the novel, but did let me down a bit with the very last chapters. And as you probably guessed, it would be very spoiler-y of me to go into detail of what bothered me and I'm trying very hard to keep this spoiler free. <del>No promises though.</del> But it <em>will</em> contain spoilers for both <em>Unearthly</em> and <em>Hallowed</em>. And no, I will not tell you who Clara ends up with. :P<br><br><em>Boundless</em> picks up right where <em>Hallowed</em> left off. Clara is getting ready to go to college, Jeffery is still missing and Clara and Tucker's future is unknown. There is a bit of a recap over the first few chapters for those of us that possess a leaky brain, which was nice. And if you didn't read the novella <em>Radiant,</em> it is later revealed what Angela was up to in Italy. While <em>Unearthly</em> held a mysterious air and <em>Hallowed</em>'s more depressing, <em>Boundless</em> felt much more grim and hopeless. There were quite a few times where I was unsure if Clara could overcome her difficulties and even when she did, there was always something else. Cynthia Hand really showed little mercy for most of the book with her plot twists, which always seemed to bring Clara nothing but grief.<br><br><strong>Things I liked:</strong><br><br>-As usual, I love Hand's writing style. There are some authors that just get a great feel for how teens talk and Hand is one of them. Also, Clara is a smartass and I love it.<br><br>-I think this book has the best plot out of the series. There is a lot more suspense going on because Clara has not one, but two visions. She's also on a time crunch, lives are on the line. You, know. Important things of that nature.<br><br>-Samjeeza's role. I have to admit, I kinda like the guy. His story is very sad and I felt for him.<br><br>-Tucker: HKFHJDNHFJBFKHJFB!!!! I loved how Clara just couldn't seem to stay away from him. His scenes gave me SERIOUS FEELS like this one:<br><br><img alt="fictional-character" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363266i/714523.jpg" width="420" height="294" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><em>I received very strange looks from Mr. Sinclair while reading Boundless.</em><br><br><strong>Things I'm not too sure about:</strong><br><br>I was really hoping that Boundless would tie up a bunch of loose threads, but it seemed to just leave more questions than answers.<br><br>-I was surprised to find out how big of a part Angela had in the storyline. Throughout the series I had my suspicions that she was evil, but she was cleverly left ambiguous until now. However, I'm not sure I like where her story arc went. Was Angela's purpose really to throw her future away?<br><br>-What in the world was Jeffery's purpose? Why did God want him to start the forest fire?<br><br>-<em>Boundless</em> is a lot more "preachy" than the first two. And when I say preachy, I mean it has a lot more religious references, including a few bible quotes and everything. I suppose some of that can't be avoided since it is an angel book, but it is there. I did find it kind of ironic that Tucker would bust out his bible on Clara. It was a human preaching to an angel. Lol.<br><br>-Tucker vs. Christian. I was not happy with their endings. It's not that I'm disappointed with who Clara ends up because I honestly would be fine with either choice. But it's how each of their story arcs ends. One just disappears from Clara's life, which is messed up because he doesn't get a decent ending. And the other experiences a big change in their life that I thought was convenient and a little too "happily-ever-after" for my liking.<br><br>The biggest issue for me had been with the ending because it felt like Clara got everything so conveniently handed to her. Don't get me wrong, Clara did go through hell in the book (quite literally actually), but when the consequences and life catches up to her, everything magically becomes alright. Somehow Clara has this power and that power. Oh and she can magically do this, but you didn't know about it till now, because secretly she's been slightly Mary Sue-ish all along. Surprise! Everyone's purpose in the series has revolved around Clara's. And these people have suffered badly, especially Angela, Christian and Tucker, the poor, little mortal.<br><br>Also, let's discuss purposes for a minute. Slight spoiler: Clara was always told by her mother that her goal in life is to always fulfill her purpose. So when she has these visions, she goes out of her way to make sure it happens. In fact, her mother was even disappointed in Clara for ignoring her visions for the better part of <em>Unearthly.</em> But later we find out that the visions are just glimpses of a possible future. So basically: You don't have to do what the vision says, but you'd better anyway because it's also your purpose? HUH? But furthermore, if all this time the angels were just seeing possible futures, why weren't any other possibilities shown?<br><br>Overall, I did enjoy Boundless. Sure, there were a few instances that I wasn't exactly thrilled about. And yeah, the ending did leave me a bit frustrated. But this book also made me laugh, cry and was never boring. It may not be the perfect ending I thought it'd be, but I certainly had fun reading it. A series has come and gone. I'm sad to see it go, but I am very excited to see what Cynthia Hand comes up with next.<br><br><em>ARC was received from the publisher. Thank you, HaperTeen!</em><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.<br><br><b>PLEASE DO NOT CLICK THE SPOILERS IN THE COMMENTS IF YOU HAVEN'T READ THE BOOK!</b><br><br>----------------<br>Before reading:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363266i/714524.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Damn you Tucker and Christian! Damn you both with your ridiculous ability to make me squeal like a swooning fangirl! Damn you to the firey pits of he---<br><br><i>*SWOON*<br><br>*drags self off floor*</i><br><br>I can't believe this. <br><br><i>Ohmygod</i><br><br>I just realized I'm not even remotely prepared for more of your awesomeness yet! <br><br>MUST.<b>GET</b>.READY.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379785040i/464883.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8523382919340352100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_304680264" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304680264" />
    <a title="Mitchii" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4808951-mitchii"><img alt="Mitchii" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605348765p2/4808951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/304680264?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitchii" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitchii" href="/user/show/4808951-mitchii">Mitchii</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808951-mitchii?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer304680264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7106555696163434831">Here's my full review (spoilers ahead):<br/><br/>Ok, you guys I’m ready to speak. I’m ready to shout it out to each and every one concern how much this book disappoints me. I know it’s unfair to judge and rate it on who Clara ended up with. It is totally and utterly unfair. But the story did treat the ‘<i>one I preferred for her</i>’ the exact same way. I wish that he wasn’t that understanding. I wish he did something awful. I wish he wasn’t that supportive of her. I wish there’s something negative to say about </span>
  <span id="freeText7106555696163434831" style="display:none">Here's my full review (spoilers ahead):<br /><br />Ok, you guys I’m ready to speak. I’m ready to shout it out to each and every one concern how much this book disappoints me. I know it’s unfair to judge and rate it on who Clara ended up with. It is totally and utterly unfair. But the story did treat the ‘<i>one I preferred for her</i>’ the exact same way. I wish that he wasn’t that understanding. I wish he did something awful. I wish he wasn’t that supportive of her. I wish there’s something negative to say about him. But I come up empty handed. Because if there’s one thing after all that has happened to them proved is that he completely, definitely and truly LOVES her. As in just her. And not because of anything else.<br /><br />Before I go to my main point, I would like to tell you good people, especially if you like the story regardless who she’ll end up with that the conclusion of this trilogy is actually well executed. Ms. Hand knitted all those lose threads. So much sometimes, I think, it crushed all the possibilities I’ve been thinking right after I read it (that is all connected to my main concern). It was so clean, so spotless that something made it a little flat to me. But overall, the story was fascinating, while yes, I would’ve changed few [major] details about it but I sincerely enjoyed majority of it.<br /><br />Now let me start with my <u>Christian Prescott centric review</u> and please if you haven’t read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13049981-boundless" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Boundless</b>
</a> and not too fond of spoilers, discontinue reading this review now. I’m about to recklessly gush and I don’t want to ruin anything for you. But if you don’t mind, then go ahead spoil to your heart’s content.<blockquote>“<strong>I love you,</strong>” he murmurs. “<strong>Can you feel that? You. Not some destiny I think I’m called to. You. I’m with you. My strength. My soul. My heart. Feel it.</strong>” – Christian to Clara</blockquote>The constant argument against Christian and Clara’s relationship is that it wasn’t love. They were just connected because of their ‘<u>purpose</u>.’ Sometimes that word irked me the most because after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110-hallowed" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Hallowed </b>
</a>ended I saw that Christian’s gestures were no longer just connected with their divine mission. While I do admit that I think that Christian and Clara’s relationship started because of it. That after he found out that Clara is also just like him triggered something in him. But it was just that he found someone he can finally share intimate details of his life who very much knows his circumstances. But more than that, I sincerely think that he fell in love with her because of the time they shared together. He finally knew who Clara was. The Clara beyond his vision. The true Clara Gardner. That she’s more than the person/angel-blood mysteriously entwined with his (their) purpose. She is just Clara. The sarcastic, fun, beautiful, and strong lady that he fell in love with.<br /><br />Yes, bottom-line is HE LOVES HER. Purpose aside, he truly loves her.<blockquote>“<strong>But there’s something about you two, when you’re together. It’s like you fit.</strong>” He grins. Shrugs. “<strong>He’s your soul mate.</strong>” – Jeffrey</blockquote>You know what I hate the most is how the story established how they fit together. How pleasant and romantic the idea of them together. It’s like all facts headed straight to point A (Christian) the suddenly it went to point B (Tucker). I don’t have anything against Tucker. I’m even on his team before, my <a href="http://bookish.skycircus.org/2011/01/18/unearthly-by-cynthia-hand/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Unearthly</b>
</a> review can attest to that. But like I said, why made Christian so damn supportive? Why show us the possibility which make a lot more sense than the time she was with Tucker? I’m here asking those questions. Still asking them. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244-unearthly" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Unearthly</b>
</a>, I was actually surprised that they ended up as an item. But it only showed how Tucker grounded Clara’s life. That it showed that her life is not driven by anyone but by herself. It’s her life, her wheel. But in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110-hallowed" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Hallowed</b>
</a>, during and after the situation she was with her mother and how Christian is there for her, it showed a lot about their potential as a couple. It says a lot about Christian as well, and the way they support each other on that moment. That they shared many things aside from their heavenly lineage. If Christian found someone who can now understand him, Clara did have that too, with Christian.<br /><br />His dedication for her in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13049981-boundless" rel="nofollow noopener"><b>Boundless</b> </a>didn’t falter. In fact, all the important events happened with Clara or with the story Christian was there. My head couldn't wrap the idea of Tucker getting the larger picture. It was lackluster and shallow reason that he is her "home." And even if Clara was indecisive and insensitive, Christian still never left her side. Even if he bends his principles, he will do it for her. And all the major events (even painful ones–especially painful ones), <u>the one person who is always there for her was Christian.</u> He had his devotion proved over and over again. He’s so unselfish. Isn’t that a characteristic of true love? But yet all he had done are now pointless because he didn’t have what he deserves. I’m not just talking about Clara. If there’s one character that should’ve a well-deserved happy ending, that’s him.<blockquote>“<strong>…Maybe I’ll catch up with you in a hundred years or so.</strong>” … He smirks. “<strong>I won’t call it waiting,</strong>” – Christian</blockquote>Ah Christian, how can you be so that? So…almost perfect. And up until now he’s still hoping. He deserves someone but my stubborn heart still aching for Clara. I don’t know but I feel that his happiness will be complete with Clara at his side. But Tucker’s new situation changed the ball game. I hope his ‘longevity’ is not as long as Methuselah. Because darn right, that will crush my already itsy bitsy hope.<br /><br />Anyway, I loved the story, while I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110-hallowed" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Hallowed</b>
</a> is the best book of the series for obvious and biased reason, I still not taking what I said back: that this series is one of the well-written angel books (or paranormal book) out there. I was actually amazed on the extent of her research for her story, even going to the places personally. It showed that she poured everything in here. I might be upset and dissatisfied, yes, but that doesn’t change the fact it was an excellent story.<br /><br /><br /><b>After reading reaction:</b><br /><br />Too many emotions. I don’t know where to start. Or how should I start. There are expected awesome moments, as well as heart-crushing ones. If you’re asking if it’s about CHRISTIAN, it is. I loved his character. So much that the ending made every bit of the book pointless. <b>
  <u>Yes, I did not like the ending</u>
</b>. While I did mentally and emotionally prepare thanks to early reviews, the reality of it still hurt pretty damn bad. <br /><br />I’m still processing everything. Sorting it out. I forewarn you that my review for Boundless will concentrate more on Christian. I don’t like Christian just because of Clara, I loved him for who he is. Him alone. And it pains me that after all he went through, the one piece that missing still not filled. Ok, I’m not making sense anymore. And btw no Tucker bashing here. I liked the dude, believe it or not. But it just doesn’t make sense to me on how little he played in this book but still got the major development. Not just in his love life but his entire being. Lucky, cowboy!<br /><br />Review will up soon. Tomorrow...I think. Too tired right now. <br /><br /><br /><b>Pre-reading Review:</b><br /><br />My heart chose Christian. Sorry Tucker. :(<br /><br />*** <a href="http://ericaorourke.typepad.com/blog/2012/03/april-scavenger-hunt.html" rel="nofollow noopener">From YA Scavenger Hunt</a>: A preview from the third book. Clara and Christian is on a date. Date! Me: hyperventilating due to excessive fangirling. Eeeeep!!! ***<br /><br />Update (May 29, 2012): Holy macaroons, there's the title. BOUNDLESS. I think I'm in love (again). &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="7106555696163434831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4581159-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322348543p2/4581159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235459902?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/4581159-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235459902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1294771522168357511">I stayed up all night finishing this last night. The ending was perfection but I took away one star because I was so bored and annoyed for most of the book because it was all Christian. I really can't say much about how I feel about the book without spoilers so... Don't read this unless you want to know who she ends up with. I knew before I started so I understand needing to know.<br/><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I loved the ending. All along we knew Christian was just a great partner and friend. Clara never reall</span></span>
  <span id="freeText1294771522168357511" style="display:none">I stayed up all night finishing this last night. The ending was perfection but I took away one star because I was so bored and annoyed for most of the book because it was all Christian. I really can't say much about how I feel about the book without spoilers so... Don't read this unless you want to know who she ends up with. I knew before I started so I understand needing to know.<br><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I loved the ending. All along we knew Christian was just a great partner and friend. Clara never really felt more for him which was evident on their one date where they were not allowed to talk about anything angel related and then they had nothing to talk about. It was always Tucker and I do think Clara gave Christian a fair shot. But she just never felt much more for him than friendship and some attraction. Anyone that follows my reviews knows I am actually usually more on Team Guy #2 but not this time. I did give Christian a shot myself but he was pushing, annoying, and never had any real chemistry with Clara. I think he took his purpose the wrong way and also thought he had to be with Clara when hey had the purpose wrong all along. I'm glad the whole purpose thing was cleared up because for someones purpose to be to get with someone just rubs me the wrong way. It makes more sense that Christiana and Clara were to team up and be strong as Triplares together but that Clara could choose Tucker. I know the whole Clara saving Tucker and turning him into a Prophet was convenient but I don't give a fig! As for Christian, Clara told him in book 1 I AM IN LOVE WITH TUCKER AVERY so everything after that was his fault for pushing her when he knew it wasn't ever going to happen. I really don't think he will sit around for a 100 years waiting for her. I'm sure he will move on. He just said that and now Tucker's lifespan is lengthened anyway. And Clara doesn't want Christian now so why would she want him after 80 years of a happy marriage with Tucker. I loved the epilogue and seeing Tucker and Clara together. I was wondering if Clara was pregnant or they had kids the way Angela asked if she wanted to borrow a parenting book?! Either way it was a great end! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>Dear dark wings/black wings/whatever the heck you call the evil angels,<br>Please eat Christian! <br><br>Dear Tucker,<br>Please fight for Clara! Christian is indeed a smug bastard!<br><br>Dear Clara, <br>Hello?! You love Tucker! Who cares about this evil purpose stuff when your brother was told to light a forest on FIRE?!?!<br><br>That is all!<br>Oh and have you read the Boundless teaser of Clara and Christian on a date. Read at own risk because I felt sick after reading it lol. But hey a least Clara is thinking of Tucker. <br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://ericaorourke.typepad.com/blog/2012/03/april-scavenger-hunt.html">http://ericaorourke.typepad.com/blog/...</a><br><br>And thank you to Asher @ <a href="http://www.paranormalindulgence.net/2012/01/joint-blog-tour-everneath-hallowed.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Paranormal Indulgence</a> for this drawing that sums up my feelings.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356342i/708026.png" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356343i/708027.png" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_268528720" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268528720" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268528720?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062103468" href="/book/show/15819317-boundless">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=all-time-faves">all-time-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=2013-faves">2013-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=i-just-have-a-lot-of-feelings">i-just-have-a-lot-of-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=heroines-i-adore">heroines-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=heroes-i-adore">heroes-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=fluffy">fluffy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=oh-my-god-marry-me">oh-my-god-marry-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=masterpiece">masterpiece</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268528720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4013464269923965091"><a href='http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2013/01/review-boundless-by-cynthia-hand.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236610i/681460.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>So. Here we are at last.<br/><br/>I don't know why good-byes are called <i>good</i>-byes, and I don't want to say it to this series. I don't want to. I don't.<br/><br/>In the desolate, barren land of YA angel fiction, the <i>Unearthly</i> series is like a beacon of light. A <i>clara lux in obscuro</i>, better yet. It is beautiful. It is heartwarming. And it may just be one of the paranormal series' I've read that I am extremely, emotionally invested on.<br/><br/>That's the main thing I love about this series, really, is that it's so <i>real</i>. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText4013464269923965091" style="display:none"><a href="http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2013/01/review-boundless-by-cynthia-hand.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236610i/681460.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So. Here we are at last.<br><br>I don't know why good-byes are called <i>good</i>-byes, and I don't want to say it to this series. I don't want to. I don't.<br><br>In the desolate, barren land of YA angel fiction, the <i>Unearthly</i> series is like a beacon of light. A <i>clara lux in obscuro</i>, better yet. It is beautiful. It is heartwarming. And it may just be one of the paranormal series' I've read that I am extremely, emotionally invested on.<br><br>That's the main thing I love about this series, really, is that it's so <i>real</i>. The writing and the dialogue between the characters is definitely something you'd find in contemporary novels. It makes the characters seem to me like actual, living people, and it makes me care about them as if I know them personally. It makes me <i>feel</i> for them.<br><br><i>Boundless</i> was a breathtaking conclusion. The same with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a>, it was a rollercoaster of emotions, only this time it's intensified. I laughed, I cried, I cheered, I yelled, I cried some more. Cynthia Hand seems to know exactly how to hit me in the feels, and splatter my emotions all over the walls.<br><br>Clara is one of my most favorite heroines. She's so damn relatable and just <i>likable</i>. I still can't exactly explain what it is about her that I love so much, but she's never once annoyed me or came across as a Mary Sue. And it helps that she's funny. I think it's pretty hard <i>not</i> to root for her, because there's just something about her.<br><br>Tucker and Christian. Tucker and Christian. These two . . . my God, I love them both so much. I honestly feel the same way about them as Clara does in the end. But I really really love both of these two. Cynthia Hand knows how to make a love triangle the <i>right</i> way, because usually I'd pick one guy and stick with him, or sometimes I'd pick neither. But this series is an exception because both guys are so amazing. Back when I read the first book, I thought Christian was just a nuisance. An obstacle. I never expected to love him as much as I do now.<br><br>And Tucker. Tucker freaking Avery. I will forever weep for the fact that you are fictional.<br><br>We're introduced to a new villain here, and a new plot line. I didn't really 100% understand what the motive of the Black Wings were here, but it wasn't something that got to me because I've always thought that the characters were the highlight of the whole series, and they're the main reason I love it as much as I do, as I said before. But the plot of the book was definitely gripping, with many shocks and heart-wrenching moments along the way.<br><br>Chapter 18 was hands down my favorite chapter of the book, though. We get a beautiful scene, and I won't give away much, but it involves Clara's mother. And I hope when you read it, it warms your heart as much as it did mine.<br><br>The ending was so perfect. So perfect that I just started bawling. They weren't just sad tears, though. They were tears for every emotion I felt when I read this book, reaching their peak and finally just bursting all at once. Joy for the beautiful way it ended. Sorrow and a little bit of anger that it's all over. And of course, undying and unconditional love.<br><br>I really wish Cynthia Hand would possibly write a prequel, telling of Clara's mother's story. For the fact that I don't want this series to end, and also because I genuinely want to know more about her, and what her life was like. Sure, we got lots of glimpses and stories of it from the series, but I'd love the full experience, from her point of view. Surely I'm not the only one who wants this, right?<br><br>This series is and will remain close to my heart. And I think I've said all I wanted to say.<br><br>And Cynthia Hand, thank you. For giving us all proof that there is still hope for YA angel fiction.<br><br>____________________________<br><br><b>Pre-review thoughts:</b>IT HAS A TITLE!!!<br><br><b>Update:</b> HOLY MOTHER FUCKING COVER OH MY FUCKING GOD COVER I CAN'T OMG HOLY FUCK SHIT HOLY PENGUINS OF THE MOTHER FUCKING WORLD OH MY GODDY GODDERSON.<br><br>That cover.<br><br>I can't breathe.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363154ra/714401.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seriously, though, LOOK AT IT. Fuck. It goes <i>beyond</i> my expectations. &lt;3 So excited for this book, but also a little sad because it's the last one.<br><br><b>Update: #2</b> Ohhhhhh not long now baby, you will be MINE. Come to meeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeeee.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4013464269923965091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353589792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3718823448463096197"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381608i/738959.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Dear God,<br/>I don't want to die. Not now.<br/>Sincerely,<br/>Clara Gardner</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This is a fairly spoiler-free review (outside of the tags), but there are some spoilers in the comments, so avoid the comments if you havent' read this.<br/><br/>That ending! If only I could tell you my thoughts about the ending! <br/><br/>For the most part, I think Ms. Hand did alright. I shamefully admit to being something of a whiny brat about the early direction of <i>Boundless</i>. There's such a thing as a comfort zone and I was not in it for t</span>
  <span id="freeText3718823448463096197" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381608i/738959.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Dear God,<br>I don't want to die. Not now.<br>Sincerely,<br>Clara Gardner</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>This is a fairly spoiler-free review (outside of the tags), but there are some spoilers in the comments, so avoid the comments if you havent' read this.<br><br>That ending! If only I could tell you my thoughts about the ending! <br><br>For the most part, I think Ms. Hand did alright. I shamefully admit to being something of a whiny brat about the early direction of <i>Boundless</i>. There's such a thing as a comfort zone and I was not in it for the first half of this installment. I honestly had troubles with the new setting and turn of events. It's sort of a pet peeve of mine when series take a turn into the future, yet I still feel stuck in the past. <br><br>But what am I complaining for? Of course I was going to be taken on a wild ride. I should have <i>known</i> not to question what was going to happen. It's the same thing I did with book 2, and I ended up dealing with everything just fine. When I know that I like an author's style, it should give me the confidence to be able to trust what's up around the bend. <br><br>There were some new twists in this installment and even a couple of small things which managed to surprise me. The back and forth with the visions was interesting, yet frustrating at times? Maybe that was just my take on it though. Even though the use of the visions added extra snippets to the story which weren't bad to read, it all seemed like a too-convenient tool to use as a method of delivery. I'm probably nit-picking a little on that though. <br><br>If you haven't tried out this series (trilogy, really), and love for your angel stories to be more on the sweet romance-y side with an extra dash of mystery and adventure, check these books out. If you want to read something darker, well...you're out of luck with this particular set of books. Even though there were technically "baddies," let's not kid ourselves here - a story with villains does not always equal dark. If you're looking for something less sweet, shoot me a message and we'll talk about darker. <br><br>At the end of it all, I can say that I am happy. I am content. I am glad that I took the journey. It's a given that I'll be checking out whatever this author decides to write in the future. Plus, she mentioned <i>Vampire Academy</i> in this book, so I had a moment of <b>let me love you</b> toward Ms. Hand. I think I can support this woman.<br><br>Totally random, but I really want to know what <i>a whiff of cloud</i> smells like. Misty air? Cotton? <br><br>My spoiler musings for those who've finished the book : <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm glad that Clara and Tucker got back together, but poor Christian. He kind of had no ending. :( Maybe he and Clara will reunite after Tucker's been dead for a while (or maybe not, since it appears Tucker's not going anywhere anytime soon). I think that's the ending I've imagined in my head. <br><br>It seemed like the Phen &amp; Angela story should have had more completion. <br><br>I wanted to know more about Jeffrey's life. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>It's been a while since I've gotten stuck writing a review and I'm not quite sure how to wrap this up. Guess it's time to just bring back a simple....<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>FIN</b>
  </i>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_419156917" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/419156917" />
    <a title="Brigid ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886144-brigid"><img alt="Brigid ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581869052p2/886144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419156917?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid ✩" href="/user/show/886144-brigid">Brigid ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=angels">angels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419156917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9830100631850654432">Okay, I have been terrible at getting reviews done, lately. Just terrible. Gosh, I read this almost two months ago, and my to-review pile is starting to verge on terrifying. Once again. <br/><br/>Well, even though I read this ages ago, I'm going to try to review it as best as I can. First, for the fangirling portion of our review:<br/><br/>AAHHHHHH. IT WAS SO GOOD AND I HAVE SO MANY FEELINGS AND AKDJF;KDSJF;LSDJFLKA.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391948ra/754661.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391948ra/754662.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ah-hem. I just had to get that out of my system. (Also, that second gif doesn't really have any rele</span>
  <span id="freeText9830100631850654432" style="display:none">Okay, I have been terrible at getting reviews done, lately. Just terrible. Gosh, I read this almost two months ago, and my to-review pile is starting to verge on terrifying. Once again. <br><br>Well, even though I read this ages ago, I'm going to try to review it as best as I can. First, for the fangirling portion of our review:<br><br>AAHHHHHH. IT WAS SO GOOD AND I HAVE SO MANY FEELINGS AND AKDJF;KDSJF;LSDJFLKA.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391948ra/754661.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391948ra/754662.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ah-hem. I just had to get that out of my system. (Also, that second gif doesn't really have any relevance. I just think it's hilarious and I wanted to use it.<br><br>On to the (slightly) more formal version of the review:<br><br>I really enjoyed this book and this series. When I picked up the first book, I hated it at first. I thought I'd gotten myself into another terrible paranormal romance in which I'd have to suffer through a weak and intolerable protagonist, a stalker love interest, insta-love galore, you name it. In the beginning, it really seemed like it was headed down that path.<br><br>As I got farther into that first book, I surprisingly found myself becoming addicted to the story, actually <i>liking</i> the characters, and found that there were a lot of twists in the plot that I did not expect at all. What had the setup to be a potentially clichéd paranormal romance ended up being quite original in a lot of subtle but important ways. The second book continued this, showing a lot of heart and some great character development.<br><br>These trends remained in the third book, which is (sadly) the conclusion to the trilogy. It's very different from the first two books, but without wandering away too much from the story and characters. <br><br>In <i>Boundless</i>, we find Clara starting out in college as she, Christian, and Angela all begin their studies at Stanford University. (Side note: I found it kind of silly and unrealistic that they all got into Stanford and all chose to go there, but oh well. I see how it was kind of necessary in order for the plot to work.) Anyway, believability issues aside, I was happy to see a YA book that actually took place in college. As a college student who still loves YA, that's something I'd like to see more of. (And I'm not counting New Adult, because I have yet to see New Adult books that are more than just "porn for teenagers." Hopefully that will change in the coming years.) <br><br>So now, Clara and her friends have to balance their college work along with dealing with evil angels (of course). Clara, Christian, and Angela are all having disturbing visions––which all seem to point to one terrifying battle and possibly Clara's death.<br><br>Of the three books, this one probably had the most amount of plot. While the first two took a while to start up, I thought the third did a good job of keeping up the pace. Sure, it was a little slow as Clara adjusted to college life and whatnot, but there were still enough hints at conflict that made it intriguing. <br><br>As I've said, it was great to see YA characters in college. But not only that, it was great to see teenage characters actually considering what they were going to do with their futures, what careers they might pursue, etc. I almost NEVER see this in YA books, especially of the paranormal variety. I just can't express how glad I was to see a paranormal YA book that didn't just center around the romance. Sure, the romance aspect is still important, but it doesn't consume the plot. We also see Clara worrying about what she's going to do once she's out of school. <br><br>I guess this is a minor spoiler, but she decides she might want to be a doctor. I mean, she has healing powers, so why not? I thought it was awesome that she actually wanted to use her powers to help people:<br><br><i>"I can't spend my entire life being afraid of the black-winged bogeymen. I have to live my life ... I won't be stupid about glory, but I won't sit around and wait for my visions to happen in order to do something with it."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391948ra/754663.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391948ra/754664.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Just ... YES. I don't think I have ever, <i>ever</i> read a YA paranormal book where the protagonist was like, "You know what? I don't care if it might get me in trouble ... I have this magical power, and I'm going to use it to help people for the rest of my life, dammit!" But it's not like she's just doing it unprofessionally either ... She's actually studying for a medical degree. It's just terrific. <br><br>(I mean, compare it to a book like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7778981.Halo__Halo___1_" title="Halo (Halo, #1) by Alexandra Adornetto" rel="nofollow noopener">Halo</a> where the main character is an angel with healing powers, yet all she does is make out with her boyfriend and whine about how she doesn't like watching the news because it "makes her depressed." Oy vey.) <br><br>I also thought that, unlike in a lot of paranormal romance books, the whole romance &amp; love triangle thing was actually handled quite well. As I mentioned earlier, even though it's significant, it doesn't take up the entire story. Sure, Clara does face some conflict in choosing between Tucker and Christian––but neither of the boys are douchebags about it; in fact, they're both quite nice. There is some jealousy here and there, but that's understandable.<br><br>Also, when Angela says something about Clara needing to pursue her destiny and be with Christian in order to complete herself or whatever, Clara says:<br><br><i>"Look, I'm a complete person … I don't need Christian to complete me."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391948ra/754665.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>THAT'S RIGHT. YOU GO, GIRL.<br><br>I also like that Cynthia Hand incorporated religion into the book without it becoming preachy. In books about angels, the issue is pretty much bound to come up at some point. And it's handled quite badly in some other angel books I've <s>suffered through</s> read. I don't know what Hand's personal beliefs are––which is good, because that means she didn't shove it down the readers' throats. The book does suggest the existence of God, but not in a way that says "God says this is right and this is wrong, etc." When the subject does come up, it's usually something like:<br><br><i>"Whoever does not love does not know God, because God is love."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/558713.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><s>None of that "Marriage is between a man and a woman" crap like in That Other Angel Book That Shall Not Be Named.</s><br><br>The only thing along those lines that I took issue with was some occasional slut-shaming, but it wasn't really related to religion. And it wasn't <i>too</i> bad. But ... still. Oh well.<br><br>I also thought Samjeeza proved to be a very interesting character. In the first two books he kind of seemed like a very typical, two-dimensional villain. But in the third book, his past involving Clara's mother became more apparent. And it got to the point where I actually felt bad for him. It was like, Clara was the only connection he had left to her mother, so she's the only one he can tell/share stories with.<br><br>And now for the spoilers section:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Parts I wanted to address in some way or another:<br><br>- Angela getting pregnant (and having a baby): WHOA, I did not see that one coming. But I thought it was kinda cool, in a way. I would like it if more YA authors showed that there can be consequences of having unprotected sex. I've read several YA books where characters had unprotected sex like it was no big deal, and nothing happened to them ... no STDs, no pregnancy. I'd like to see more YA authors address the issue of protected vs. unprotected sex and pregnancy, etc. But anyway, Angela getting pregnant wasn't some kind of PSA, either. I think it helped her to develop a lot as a character, and it was significant to the plot. <br><br>- Jeffrey's whole relationship with Lucy and how she turned out to be evil and everything: Eh, I was not really a fan of this. It was just SO OBVIOUS, it was almost painful. I mean, come on:<br><br>Jeffrey: "Yeah, I'm thinking a bird [tattoo] on my shoulder, like a hawk or something."<br>Lucy: "Maybe a raven."<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391948ra/754666.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah, it's not like you have been using a raven as a sign of evil throughout the whole series. Anyway, moving along ...<br><br>- The scene where Clara visits her mom in the past: TEARS, JUST TEARS EVERYWHERE. I COULDN'T HANDLE MY FEELS.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391948ra/754667.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Acck it was just so beautiful.<br><br>- In hell, there's an evil tattoo parlor where people get their sins tattooed on them: AWESOME. That was just ... awesome. I thought it was a really cool idea.<br><br>- Angela and Christian are half-siblings: DAYUMMM. Well, that would explain the whole thing where they kissed (in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15851966.Radiant__Unearthly___2_5_" title="Radiant (Unearthly, #2.5) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Radiant</a>) and Angela was like, "Eew, it felt like I was kissing my brother." Well played, Cynthia Hand.<br><br>- Okay, the ending. Hmm. I had very mixed feelings about it. I mean, sure I was happy Clara ended up with Tucker. I like Tucker. It was sweet and everything. It just felt a little convenient to me that he became semi-immortal and all. Also, I felt like Christian just kind of got cast aside. It sucks how in a lot of these love triangle scenarios, one of the guys basically gets totally forgotten at the end. It had a rather Hunger Games-esque annoying flash-forward endings where it was like, "La di da, here's the future where we're married and have kids. And what happened to that other guy? Oh, who knows. He's around somewhere. Whatevs." So, that kind of pissed me off. But, oh well. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Over all, I thought this was a great conclusion to the series, which was both heartfelt and exciting. I really enjoyed reading it, and I'm eager to see what Cynthia Hand does next!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9830100631850654432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290403594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12915166868093075677"><b>
  <u>After Reading:</u>
</b><br/>It's difficult to say what I think about this book.<br/>I made it <i>quite</i> obvious that I am on Team Tucker.<br/>So if I start ranting and bursting into tears <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Although I did burst into tears when Cynthia Hand <i>almost</i> pulled an Andrea Cremer (you probably have no idea what that is...) <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> you might assume that Clara chose Christian.<br/>If I get all bubbly and happy, you might assume that Clara chose Tucker.<br/>Let's just say that this book gave me <i>all the feels</i>.<br/>There were t</span>
  <span id="freeText12915166868093075677" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>After Reading:</u>
</b><br />It's difficult to say what I think about this book.<br />I made it <i>quite</i> obvious that I am on Team Tucker.<br />So if I start ranting and bursting into tears <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Although I did burst into tears when Cynthia Hand <i>almost</i> pulled an Andrea Cremer (you probably have no idea what that is...) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> you might assume that Clara chose Christian.<br />If I get all bubbly and happy, you might assume that Clara chose Tucker.<br />Let's just say that this book gave me <i>all the feels</i>.<br />There were times of crying, times of ranting.<br />There were times where I wanted to hug everyone, times of laughter.<br />But it wasn't one or the other! I had all those feels!<br /><br />This was an amazing series that I have a feeling that I will re-read again and again.<br />Get all those feels again and again.<br />Am I happy about how it ended? Maybe. Like I said, my feeling towards the end may tell you who Clara ends up with (and I don't want to ruin it for you!)<br />But I am sad that it <i>ended</i>.<br />There will be no more Unearthly books...<br />but every series must end at some point and in a week or so I might get over this loss...maybe.<br />But I thank you, Unearthly, for giving me the feels.<br />And I thank you, Cynthia Hand, for writing such an amazing book.<br />So, now I must say... Goodbye, Unearthly.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Before Reading:</u>
</b><br />*Ahem*<br />Clara, Tucker, you guys are really annoying me.<br />stop with the whole breaking up thing and get back together (and excuse me for being cliche) but you guys belong together.<br />And Clara, forget about Christian. You guys have nothing (no offence to "Team Christian") you just think you belong together because the big guy up there seems to be steering you in that direction.<br />don't listen to him<br /><b>HE CAN'T TELL YOU WHAT TO DO!!</b><br />*looks up at the sky*<br />no offence big guy<br />But Clara, the laws of the universe are clearly saying that you belong with Tucker and not Christian.<br /><b>THE LAWS OF THE UNIVERSE DO NOT LIE!</b><br />You and Christian probably wouldn't be interested in each other if it weren't for your "purpose" (and yeah okay, the half angel thing might have something to do with it too but that's not the point!)<br />Anywho....<br />Tucker not Christian <br /><br />Oh and.....<br /><b>WHY MUST THIS COME OUT AFTER THE WORLD ENDS?!!!</b><br />*cries*<br /><br />That is all<br /><br />P.S. I don't usually pick "Teams" so i'm also not usually like this...<br /><br /><b>EDIT: YAY! There's a title now and an actual release date! (sorta)<br />*jumps up and down with happiness*</b><br /><br /><br /><b>EDIT: OH MY! OH MY! OH MY!<br />That cover!<br />It's so beautiful!!<br />I'm actually having tears of joy from seeing this cover!!<br />It's just so amazing!!<br />and we're getting one step closer to the release!!</b><br /><br /><b>ANOTHER EDIT:</b><br />FALSE ALARM!!!<br />The world didn't end!<br /><br />Come to me January!!!!!!!<br /><br /><b>EDIT NUMBER 3:</b><br />Okay..okay...okay...<br />I was going to buy this THE DAY IT CAME OUT BUT...<br />Now i'm having seconds thoughts.<br />I'm so so <i>so</i> scared of what might happen in this book!<br />WHAT IF CLARA ENDS UP WITH CHRISTIAN?!!!!<br /><br />I'M SERIOUS!!!<br />I. AM. FREAKING. OUT. RIGHT. NOW.<br />If Clara ends up with Christian I don't know if I can take it!!!!<br />What would happen is that I will end out hating the book and continue my hate onwards to THE WHOLE SERIES!! I wouldn't be able to look at an Unearthly book without either glaring or bursting into tears!!<br />Please please PLEASE don't choose Christian, Clara!!!!!!!!<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I'm still going to read the book.<br />But i'm going to play it safe by checking it out of the library...<br /><br />P.S. DO NOT CHOOSE CHRISTIAN!!!!!!!! ARE YOU HEARING ME, CLARA? CHOOSE TUCKER!!!!!!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12915166868093075677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
