<div id="review_972950675" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/972950675" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/972950675?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">If you like angels... ❤</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=rivalities">rivalities</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=angels">angels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer972950675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer712478498443869996"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403380743i/10086678._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='360' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What a conclusion to this Unearthly trilogy! <b>Must say Cynthia Hand is clever, as I was more than impressed with the plot she created.</b> There was always something in every one of her books that completely surprised me and that I was not expecting. Why it is such a great thing is that, in YA series, it can be hard sometimes to not predict the events and endings since a lot has been done already. Angels are actually a very popular subject that many authors already exploited. The fact that the author</span>
  <span id="freeText712478498443869996" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1403380743i/10086678._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What a conclusion to this Unearthly trilogy! <b>Must say Cynthia Hand is clever, as I was more than impressed with the plot she created.</b> There was always something in every one of her books that completely surprised me and that I was not expecting. Why it is such a great thing is that, in YA series, it can be hard sometimes to not predict the events and endings since a lot has been done already. Angels are actually a very popular subject that many authors already exploited. The fact that the author succeeded to stand out means that, not only does she have talent, but she also put some visible time and effort in this final book. <b>I was not disappointed.</b><br><br><b>I’d suggest for you to read the novella named Radiant before reading Boundless and after reading Hallowed because there are many references to it.</b> I haven’t in fact read it myself but wished I did. Everything would have been clearer and, when I was surprised to discover a new angel character, I shouldn’t have since he technically is presented in that novella with an alternative point of view of Clara and Angela.<br><br>The Unearthly series is a GEM in its category. If you haven’t started it already, get to it soon, I politely say.<br><br>Clara is such an endearing character. <b>She’s the kind of main character that you can truly connect with and maybe even imagine yourself in her place by moments.</b> It’s even easier to do so since this series <b>is narrated in a first person point of view.</b> Sure, she can be sarcastic, impulsive, careless and reckless but that’s just human behaviour. No one is perfect. Overall, I think you’ll like her and want to now more about her. Personally, I would have loved to have her as part in my life, maybe as a friend.<br><br>There is still a love triangle in Boundless as in the other books. It’s still blurred but things are surely different. Clara feels the pressure to choose Christian since it is part of her mission when she, herself, actually doesn’t know if he IS her soul mate and the one she’s supposed to be with. The only thing she knows is that she still cares for Tucker (which we will still se in this book) but <b>she can’t be with him in order to keep him save.</b> Boy I was eager to know who would conquer her heart by the end of the story.<br><br>A problem I had is with Angela. You all know how bossy and how very self-confident she his. Well…I wished to slap her at least like…during my whole reading. Ugh, Angela, could you just stop thinking and listen to someone else for once? <b>Unwanted things happened to you and maybe, maybe, if you had listened to Clara, at least, it would/could have been better.</b> Angela and Clara are ‘friends’ but, to me, it’s like the only reason they are close is because of the whole angel situation which keeps bringing them together. Not a true friendship. Clara is caring but Angela is too independent also to fully let Clara in her life and open up.<br><br><b>I loved the writing and the atmosphere, a dreamy and nice one, a good contrast since a lot of events are happening in Boundless and they can get overwhelming.</b> It’s fast-paced and I, without lying, always wanted to know what was going to happen and how. The setting is also interesting since it takes mostly place on the Stanford University grounds. It was fun to meet new characters which brought a breath of fresh air in this book. Overall, it’s a must read and a series to not only pass by but to actually read. I believe it enjoyable for adults also since it is a charming, entertaining and, yes, also sad story.<br><br>Also posted on <a href="http://seeingnight.blogspot.ca/2014/06/review-of-boundless-by-cynthia-hand.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Seeing Night Reviews</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="712478498443869996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_607347619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/607347619" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/607347619?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=read-only-when-running-out-of-book">read-only-when-running-out-of-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=are-you-kidding-me">are-you-kidding-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=bad-bad-bad-romance">bad-bad-bad-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=over-my-dead-body">over-my-dead-body</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=chinese-translation">chinese-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=no-hell-no">no-hell-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=only-when-it-is-for-free">only-when-it-is-for-free</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=what-the-hell">what-the-hell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=mary-sue-warning">mary-sue-warning</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer607347619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13101136253382081317">Pre-review:<br/><br/>I have been wondering forever why everyone else seems to love this series so much. For god's sake, Clara is a Mary Sue and she's too airhead not to be annoying; the love triangle is ridiculous, the bad guys are laughing stocks at best, and there's nothing new or angelic about those holier-than-thou angel-bloods (half-angels).<br/><br/>A friend of mine stated that most people who gave four or five stars rates/reviews to this book because: (1) they had just suffered the horror of Hush, Hush, Halo</span>
  <span id="freeText13101136253382081317" style="display:none">Pre-review:<br /><br />I have been wondering forever why everyone else seems to love this series so much. For god's sake, Clara is a Mary Sue and she's too airhead not to be annoying; the love triangle is ridiculous, the bad guys are laughing stocks at best, and there's nothing new or angelic about those holier-than-thou angel-bloods (half-angels).<br /><br />A friend of mine stated that most people who gave four or five stars rates/reviews to this book because: (1) they had just suffered the horror of Hush, Hush, Halo or Fallen; (2) the supposedly 'good' writing (okay, I admit it really is better than Fallen, etc) tricked them into overlooking all the flaws: the cliches, the lack of action, the annoying love triangle and the Mary Sue main character. And goodness, the writing isn't <i>that</i> good nor interesting to me anyway. <br /><br /><i>Edited@13/01/2016</i><br /><br />I am half way through the book now, and I found something really hateful and ugly in the story:<br /><br />For the second time in this series, the author tells me a certain young girl's <b>one true and sacred purpose in life</b> is to get herself knocked up and give birth to a....you guessed it! <b>a male infant!</b> <br /><br />Holy mother fucker. The first time shits like this happen is when the author reveals <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Clara's mother's one true and sacred purpose in life is to get herself knocked up and give birth to Clara. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I can't even.<br /><br />Secondly, another young woman predictably turns out to be a villain because....you just know that having tattoos on her skin, dressing in revealing outfits and having an open attitude toward guys usually signals that she is a bad female.<br /><br /><b>Actual review starts here</b><br /><br />I almost wanted to give <i>Boundless</i> two stars, but after taking the slut shaming, the Mary Sue heroine, the extremely poorly done mythology, the plot holes, the insufferable conservative messages and the anticlimactic ending into consideration, I decided nothing more than 1 star should be given. <br /><br />Let's do a breakdown here:<br /><br /><b>(1) the Mary Sue heroine:</b> she is beautiful, she is good at everything she does, she hasn't even gotten ill in her life, she has two hot boys drooling over hear, her father is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Arch Angel Micheal, for crying out loud <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, she has power which hardly anyone else can wield, even her mother told her how special she is. <br /><br />I want to throw up.<br /><br /><b>(2) the paper-thinned mythology:</b> we are just supposed to accept that God and angels and demons exist, and the whole Christian mythology about heaven and hell is true. The God/angels are good and the demons are just bad and evil. We should just swallow it all down, no question asked. Hardly anything gets an explanation.<br /><br />In this book, Hell/underworld is mentioned, but once again we learn barely anything about it and the description of angels/demons/Hell is mind-breakingly flat and unimaginative and down right boringgggggg.<br /><br /><b>(3) the holier-and-better-than-thou-lowly-humans-angels/half angels:</b> Not only the angels and their offspring are beautiful, smart and good at everything they do, and they can't even get sick! Plus each of them has a special, God-given holy 'purpose' they need to fulfill. <br /><br />What are those holy purposes? Ending world hunger? Bringing peace to the world? Protecting humans? Nap. From what I can see their purposes directed them to hook up (God obviously loves match-making a lot) and have babies together, or to be a good citizen to their community. <br /><br />Yes...very holy, special and important purposes indeed. Not to mention female half-angels' purpose in life are to hook up with guys so they can make babies together!<br /><br /><b>(4) The slut shaming:</b> As mentioned above, wearing revealing clothes makes you a bad female.<br /><br /><b>(5) The Love Triangle: </b> Oh yes the love triangle......and this time Love Interest No. 2 Tucker is out of the picture for most time.<br /><br /><b>(6) The lack of explanation:</b> Why would the arch villain <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[wants Angela's baby so much and go into such length to catch him?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It isn't even explained!<br /><br /><b>(7) The insufferable conservatism: </b> 3 books go by, and I can't remember seeing one black angel or an Asian one (Okay, I could happen to overlook them, because the main crew is...white?). Not only this, I can't remember seeing an angel/half-angel who is anything less than middle classed. None of them do grass-root job for a living, no one lives in a poor community. I mean, screw all the 'staying with the poor and the weak' dogmas!<br /><br /><b>(8) ...and the heroine just let her 16 years old brother live by himself?</b> I mean, they are now without parents! Their mother <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[had just freaking died! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But Clara the heroine just up and goes to college and let her troubled and sad younger brother live by himself and drop out of school!?<br /><br />I don't think this is an awful book, it is only an awfully forgettable and unimaginative YA paranormal book about a Super Special Mary Sue, A Bad Love Triangle, A Bunch Of Very Special White Middle Class <s>People</s>Angels and Villains Who Hardly Do Anything Scary.<br /><br />Review for Book 1: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110-hallowed">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13101136253382081317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6714961087357046893">It's over.. Sniff<br/><br/>I really liked this ending. Though I found the beginning to be really really slow, it started to pick up in the middle and things finally moved along. Clara finally decides who she wants and it's no surprise who she picks. I did like the fact that she knew who she really wanted even though she tried giving the other one a chance. This is one of those better love triangle romances that I didn't mind who she ended up with. Also, the ending had some twists and turns and I was reall</span>
  <span id="freeText6714961087357046893" style="display:none">It's over.. Sniff<br /><br />I really liked this ending. Though I found the beginning to be really really slow, it started to pick up in the middle and things finally moved along. Clara finally decides who she wants and it's no surprise who she picks. I did like the fact that she knew who she really wanted even though she tried giving the other one a chance. This is one of those better love triangle romances that I didn't mind who she ended up with. Also, the ending had some twists and turns and I was really scared when one part ended.<br /><br />So many feels, this trilogy is written well and I can't wait to read Cynthia's next project. </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_356997783" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/356997783" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1489224-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338449051p2/1489224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/356997783?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/1489224-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=paranormal-romance-urban-fantasy">paranormal-romance-urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer356997783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12616104544032013084"><b>Spoilers for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_' title='Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unearthly</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_' title='Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hallowed</a>. Do not click on the spoiler links unless you've read <i>Boundless</i>.</b><br/><br/>Once again I find myself having mixed feelings about an <i>Unearthly</i> book, although this time my feelings were much clearer than with the last. In my opinion, this was the weakest of the series, though Cynthia Hand's engaging narrative style still makes it a quick and enjoyable read despite its flaws.<br/><br/>While I certainly found myself much more frustrated with Clara in this book than in the first two, I </span>
  <span id="freeText12616104544032013084" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a>. Do not click on the spoiler links unless you've read <i>Boundless</i>.</b><br /><br />Once again I find myself having mixed feelings about an <i>Unearthly</i> book, although this time my feelings were much clearer than with the last. In my opinion, this was the weakest of the series, though Cynthia Hand's engaging narrative style still makes it a quick and enjoyable read despite its flaws.<br /><br />While I certainly found myself much more frustrated with Clara in this book than in the first two, I can't help but love her voice. She's still very relatable, and I adore her humor and moments of self-deprecation and self-awareness, which is lacking in many YA PNR heroines. I also rediscovered my love for Jeffery in <i>Boundless</i>. I concur with other reviewers that he would make for a good spinoff character if Hand wants to revisit the <i>Unearthly</i> universe at some point. Clara's relationship with her mother, which is consistently awesome in all three books, is still compelling. Maggie would also be another good choice for a spinoff character. I would love to learn more about her life and her relationship with Samjeeza. <br /><br />Many of the issues I had with <i>Boundless</i> began in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a> and either continued on or became more extreme. Although the <i>Unearthly</i> trilogy has had an element of wish fulfillment from the beginning, it was tempered in the first book by Clara's relative inadequacies and weaknesses. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a>, these weaknesses were minimized with the revelation that she's a Triplare and the daughter of the archangel, Michael, but at least she still had to struggle with her powers. In <i>Boundless</i> we learn that not only is Clara a Triplare, she's even powerful for a Triplare. She masters new skills much more easily than other angels, and when her powers fail, it seems more like a plot contrivance than a genuine struggle because of how easily they came to her in the first place. <br /><br />I also felt that this book had more of a moral agenda than the previous two, although it was much more subtle than in other books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7778981.Halo__Halo___1_" title="Halo (Halo, #1) by Alexandra Adornetto" rel="nofollow noopener">Halo</a>. As the trilogy has developed, the mythology has relied more and more on Christian theology. In the third book one message that is telegraphed very strongly is the importance of believing in God. Evil corrupts one character by getting him/her to stop believing in God and he/she literally ends up in hell because of it. There is also an unplanned pregnancy in which there are implicit messages about how it should be handled and viewed. The entire pregnancy storyline really put a bad taste in my mouth. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Once again we have another example in YA lit where a girl gives up her future to have a child and ends up content with the outcome despite her drive and ambition. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> There's also some subtle messages about sex. In one example, Clara becomes outraged at the suggestion that she might sleep with Christian on their first date. She emphatically lets it be known she's not "that" kind of girl, which reeks of judgment. <br /><br />The mythology continued to be an issue, starting with Glory, which becomes much too convenient. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It can literally be anything the angel/angel-blood wants it to be, and it can be channeled and localized taking away its only weakness, which was that it could expose those who used it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Then there's the whole idea of ambivalent angels introduced in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15851966.Radiant__Unearthly___2_5_" title="Radiant (Unearthly, #2.5) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Radiant</a>. How can an angel be ambivalent? Being ambivalent in and of itself is going against God. It suggests angels have free will, which is what is supposed to separate angels from humans according to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And how exactly is Phen ambivalent if he's working for the Black Wings? Further, why does he not become a Black Wing after he sleeps with Angela and gets her pregnant out of wedlock? It's a sin for angels to sleep with humans, except when ordained by God (Michael and Maggie, and apparently Maggie's mother and Uriel) and at least in the case of Michael and Maggie, they were married first. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I also don't understand why the angels aren't fighting this battle with the Black Wings. Why send angel-bloods to do what a full-blooded angel could do much more efficiently? It's not as though the Black Wings aren't getting involved and angels have been known battle evil (Michael is the Smiter after all). <br /><br />Finally, the love triangle was a huge disappointment, not because of who Clara ends up with but the journey she takes to get there. I came into this book with neutral feelings about the triangle, and I thought that I would be fine with whoever Clara ended up choosing <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was almost certain after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a> that it would be Tucker, so it wasn't a huge surprise <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. As stated in my reviews of the previous books, I liked both love interests and I thought Clara had amazing chemistry with both of them. Hand could have easily written the love story in such a way that I would have been happy with either choice. Instead, it was written in such a way that it didn't matter who she ended up with, I would have been unsatisfied. Clara's back and forth between Tucker and Christian was very frustrating, especially since I thought it was clear very early on who Clara would end up with. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Clara only thinks of Tucker (and dreams only of him) and shows no romantic feelings for Christian. This didn't make much sense given her overwhelming attraction to Christian in the previous books. It's odd that she fails to overcome her feelings for Christian while she's with Tucker but once she's single, she can barely muster even a spark. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And despite the prominence of the love triangle, there weren't any real swoonworthy scenes between Clara and either boy. I thought the chemistry was lacking with both of them.<br /><br />All three characters suffer because of the love triangle. Clara's refusal to make a decision and let either of them go, thereby hurting them both, reflects poorly on her, and neither Christian nor Tucker holds her accountable for her actions. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Christian ends up looking very pathetic and I felt sorry for him. It was painful to watch him get rejected over and over again. I feel really bad for the Christian/Clara fans. There was no payoff for that ship. Tucker ends up being little more than a love interest, and an overly perfect one at that. Even though Clara has broken his heart and cheated on him, he isn't angry with her for it. Instead, he's angry because she doesn't want to have contact with him. And when she very rudely tells him they can't be friends he responds by saying she deserves to be happy. No matter how many times she rejects either of them, they both go crawling back to her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> As for the resolution itself, I thought things ended a bit too neatly for Clara and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tucker. He is saved by Clara's love, a played out YA trope, and gets to be "slightly more than human," which means magic has cured him of his sickness to her glory and it allows him to live a longer than normal life so the age difference won't be an issue. It's all too convenient for my tastes. It also annoyed me that Christian spends the rest of his life in love with Clara, unable to move on (or so it's implied). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Even though I was unhappy with the direction this series took, I still enjoyed myself. It was a quick read and I would recommend it to others with reservations. <br /><br />Nitpicky issues:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1) It bothers me that Tucker attends UC Santa Clara, a school that doesn't exist, when all of the other characters attend real colleges. It's not as though there aren't other universities near Stanford, namely San Jose State. <br />2) Angela's bright white wings are never addressed. Were they an illusion? It's explained that Christian's wings have black in them because his Black Wing father marked his soul, but Angela's are bright white even though they have the same father. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="12616104544032013084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_300185669" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300185669" />
    <a title="Booknut" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6917862-booknut"><img alt="Booknut" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411194489p2/6917862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300185669?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Booknut" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Booknut" href="/user/show/6917862-booknut">Booknut</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300185669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17918583455648025775"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380373224ra/726720.gif' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In which I discover that cliches <i>do exist</i>, as do exceptions to <i>every</i> rule and girls always pick the guy they <i>can't</i> be with.<br/><br/>Because the females of the fictional world seem to be lacking in logic. But they make up for it with enough scruples, near-death experiences, daddy-mummy issues, conflicted pasts and plain old everyday drama to fill a land fill. <br/><br/>So you see that our lovely angelic girl-wonder has come back from a trip abroad. And you're now thinking that this sounds great, right? Wrong. <br/><br/>Becau</span>
  <span id="freeText17918583455648025775" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380373224ra/726720.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In which I discover that cliches <i>do exist</i>, as do exceptions to <i>every</i> rule and girls always pick the guy they <i>can't</i> be with.<br><br>Because the females of the fictional world seem to be lacking in logic. But they make up for it with enough scruples, near-death experiences, daddy-mummy issues, conflicted pasts and plain old everyday drama to fill a land fill. <br><br>So you see that our lovely angelic girl-wonder has come back from a trip abroad. And you're now thinking that this sounds great, right? Wrong. <br><br>Because as you continue into this book, you will be constantly wishing that Cynthia Hand had spent 438 pages describing Clara's Italian Holiday, than describing Clara's American Love-wreck.<br><br>Christian appears:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380373224ra/726721.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And damn, that boy could make hippy clothes look good. He's so sweet, kind, thoughtful and downright adorable, and Clara (as per usual) is...<br><br>Moping.<br><br>Why? Because:<br> - Tucker<br> - Tucker<br> - Tucker<br> - Tucker<br> - <s>PMS</s> Tucker<br><br>Nevermind that Christian basically puts everything on hold to be with her, make her happy, protect her and be the man at her side. Clara likes guys who feel sick at the sight of her (literally, btw - her glory stuff makes him queasy), could get killed if they hang out with her, aren't going to live for as long as she will and like horses. <br><br>Now, I'm a bit of a horse girl myself (and Tucker is basically a hot, strapping ranch-raised lad right off <i>The Saddle Club</i>) but even I can take a hint when everything is shouting at me that YOU AND THIS BOY ARE NOT MEANT TO BE TOGETHER, GIRL!<br><br>Now...if Clara was ME, she would have realised that Tucker's 'edgy-bad-ass-I-hate-you-leave-me-alone' act is just that...an act. He's trying to play hard to get! And it doesn't help your 'women's lib' goals when you TELEPORT INTO HIS BARN EVERY SINGLE DAY. By 'accident'. Really, Clara? And like Tucker could stay grumpy at you for that long. The guy's a softy! He's totally putting on an act and you, Clara - you fell for it hook, line and sinker.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380373224ra/726722.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Actually, about Clara for a sec, and her constantly mentioned 'women's liberation' attitude...<br><br>Uh, where is it exactly?<br><br>Christian mentions that he's 'paying' for dinner and a movie and for her to let him even though he knows she wants to be an 'independent woman'.<br>Clara is mulling over her relationships (note the plural, because she is so, so CLINGY) and then berates herself for not being more 'women's lib' on the issue.<br>Clara likes to badmouth 'men' (as a whole) with her friend who <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[basically hooked up with a BAD ANGEL, got knocked up, hides the truth about the kid's real parent and yet even after hooking up with the BAD ANGEL goes and hooks up with a different dude <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, so she's totally one to lay the blame of stupidity on the opposite gender.<br>Clara's daddy teaches her to swordfight. So she can defend herself!<br>Clara doesn't need no man. She can watch movies on her own-wait a second, she wants to call Christian over for company...hang on, Tucker's at the door! So much for that.<br><br><b>Clara. Is. Annoying.</b><br><br>Which is the biggest shame of them all! I LOVED Clara in the other two books. But from book two to book three, for me, it felt like she needed to seriously sort out her priorities. Yeah, her life's hard. But she needs to stop abusing what she has. For e.g., her brother comes to see her after chucking a disappearing act. DON'T YELL AND BERATE HIM YOU IDIOT!! Because THAT always works well, doesn't it Clara? No wonder he left. Clara tries too hard to be in charge, that she alienates other people. She makes decision on behalf of Christian. IMPORTANT decisions. LIFE OR DEATH decisions. She has an on-off relationship with Tucker that SHE controls whether it's on or off.<br><br>She has the guys whipped!<br><br>And her treatment of Christian can be summed up as so: manipulation.<br><br>Why?<br>Because it just is.<br>Because the poor guy risks everything.<br>The dude goes out of his way.<br>He protects her.<br>Loves her.<br>Saves her.<br>Worries over her.<br>Is by her side 24/7.<br>Never ever leaves her when she needs him.<br>Aids her.<br>Would follow her to hell!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373224i/726723.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And yet...and YET...she never ever says, "Look, Christian, I really love Tucker and I think it's going to be hard for forget him. If possible, can we please still be friends. I don't want you getting the wrong idea, or feel like I'm leading you on or anything. You're important to me and I couldn't make it through half these obstacles without you. But I love Tucker. Even though we're over."<br><br>Instead, she allows him to take her on dates, to near-kiss her, to feel as if he has a chance...! When she's secretly teleporting into Tucker's barn (BY ACCIDENT), pining over Tucker, crying over Tucker, dreaming about Tucker...I could go on. But I won't. Because I am now quivering with indignation over Clara's treatment of Christian!!! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380373224ra/726724.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I need another book. You know...when Tucker's out of the picture (*cough* dead *cough*) and Clara is maturer than she is now and Christian is able to have his knight-in-shining-armour moment. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I'm not going to tell you who she finally chooses (of IF she chooses), but what I will say is that this book could have been brilliant if Clara had developed more as a character. The signs of development were there, the plot developed (really well too, actually) and the other characters developed (NB: Christian, Angela, Jeffrey). <br><br>But Clara still needed a bit more...something. I can't put it into words. That something was there when she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[used her glory sword on a very, very bad fallen angel who shall remain nameless so this spoiler isn't TOO spoiler-ish <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but it needed to have appear more often, in my opinion.<br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_514719749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/514719749" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/514719749?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

          marked it as dnf

<div id="review_264097947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/264097947" />
    <a title="Eunice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice"><img alt="Eunice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541224995p2/6078895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/264097947?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eunice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eunice" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice">Eunice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=damn-gorgeous-males">damn-gorgeous-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=nephilim-angels">nephilim-angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=i-cried-over">i-cried-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=out-2013">out-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=tear-jerking">tear-jerking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=death-tragedy-suicide">death-tragedy-suicide</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer264097947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8114831828869583268">Finally, after days undergoing the five stages of loss and grief, (Uhmm, I think I still haven't gotten that close to the fifth step) I'm calm enough to form some coherent thoughts and explanations about what I think of this final book of the Unearthly series. This still has some major ranting but I really did try to be objective here. So here we go. <br/><br/>Spoilers ahead.<br/><br/>After reading this I have to say that this series will always be one of my most favorite angel books even if it cause quite a major </span>
  <span id="freeText8114831828869583268" style="display:none">Finally, after days undergoing the five stages of loss and grief, (Uhmm, I think I still haven't gotten that close to the fifth step) I'm calm enough to form some coherent thoughts and explanations about what I think of this final book of the Unearthly series. This still has some major ranting but I really did try to be objective here. So here we go. <br /><br />Spoilers ahead.<br /><br />After reading this I have to say that this series will always be one of my most favorite angel books even if it cause quite a major heartache on me (later on that). Each aspects of the story - the character developments, the emotional depths, the plot line and the world-building were just fantastic! I finished this in one day, I couldn't really put it down. I adored almost every part of it. And Hand's writing is definitely exceptional especially since she never failed to reach me in an emotional level that mostly only contemporary books could do. I felt the hurt, the love, the regrets, the happiness, the loss, the acceptance in each of every characters. Despite its paranormal setting the emotional situations were very realistic. The development of the characters and their relationships (especially the parental love) was something I have to give Hand a very great credit for. It was wonderful and full of profound and poignant insights. <br /><br />However as much I loved almost everything about it there is this one aspect, a pretty big aspect in this book that I think Hand wasn't able to completely handle very well: the romance. The reason that left me feeling conflicted, unsettled and hurt after finishing the story. <br /><br />I am on the other team. Yes, the team whom Clara didn't choose. <i>But</i> I am not complaining because of her choice or more likely, Hand's choice. What made me disappointed and sad was <i>the way</i> it was <i>handled</i>. I have encountered countless stories with love-triangles, may it be a novel, a movie, a tv series, an anime or manga but never did I feel so bitter and broken than I had in Boundless. I could be really accepting and understanding if convinced, if it gave me reasons to believe that it has to be <i>this guy</i> and not the one I want. However that's where the problem in Boundless came. Hand failed to convince me and make me believe that Clara did the right decision by choosing Tucker but successfully and completely sold me to the idea of Clara and Christian together (and it isn't just me but a whole lot of readers too). <br /><br />The first question that popped out on my mind after reading this was what was all that about then? Hand took a lot of time polishing, emphasizing and building up Clara and Christian's relationship in this novel. And that's what I wish she never did. 'Cause you see what was the point if in the end it they wouldn't be together? (Unless Hand plans to write something about them like 80 years later). What's worse was that <i>she actually made a great job with it</i>, it was very convincing that personally I think even the Tucker fans could accept the idea of Clara and Christian. And that if she went straight in that direction I can see that she'd be able to pull it off and make a really wonderful conclusion. <br /><br />I wish she didn't make Christian a very great guy, always so supportive and understanding. I wish she didn't make Christian say all those wonderful words of adoration and love. I wish she didn't make him the perfect hero for Clara. Because seriously, all of it were pretty pointless when I reached the ending. I don't get why she has to do that. Look, I don't have a problem with Tucker. He was a great and wonderful character too, it was just that I wish Hand put a lot of more effort in him, in making me see that he had greater connection to Clara and that he was indeed her "home" so at least my heart, my poor, fragile heart wouldn't have been too hopeful and confident. <br /><br />In the end, more questions just arose in me. More notably is <i>What really is Christian to Clara?</i> Her assistant? Her freaking sidekick? Someone who'd lend her power? Her personal body guard? Well, I sound bitter on that but I just can't help it. Clara and Christian had a really strong and firm connection. Putting everything together from the first book to Boundless, it just didn't make any sense. With the way everything turned out and with that <i>convenient</i> twist in the last part it seems really unfair for Christian. He went from being a very major character, a very essential one to someone who wasn't even present on the supposedly "happy" epilogue. <br /><br />While I enjoyed most part of this book I can't say that I was satisfied with how things turned out. At some point, during those days I was processing what I really feel about this book I wanted to shout that this book is a freaking tease! Haha! Or maybe it really is. The ending did blow in my face like a sucker punch. I wish Hand could come up with another novel or even a novella just to explain everything and hopefully could give us our much needed closure. <br /><br /><br /><b>Initial Thoughts After Reading</b><br /><br />I wouldn't question the brilliant level of poignancy and profundity in this book. I was touched and moved in so many ways while reading this. The emotional depth of this story was just plain wonderful and downright amazing. However, I couldn't help feeling some qualms and apprehensiveness about the authenticity and the naturalness of the things that happened around the last parts of the book (yeah, I'm talking about the romance). It left me conflicted and had me questioning what were the purpose of some things. Like, what were all those build-up and convincing (from a lot of characters actually) for? It makes me think that they were pretty pointless with how things turned out. So you see, I really have this one big question popping out of my head after reading this book. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>So what was all <i>THAT</i> for?</b>
</blockquote><br />To those who've read this you know what I'm referring to. And I'm being pretty objective here. I really like this story and I consider this one of my most favorite angel-book. It's just hard not to wonder <i>why</i> the sudden left turn when more than half part of the book is pushing and taking us in a straight direction? And because of that the last part kinda felt a little forced for me. *sigh* I really don't know if I'm making sense. But yeah, I guess I need to process thoroughly everything out first.<br /><br />This review is also posted at <a href="http://bookoverdose.blogspot.com/2013/01/review-boundless-unearthly-3-by-cynthia.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Overdose</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8114831828869583268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1701778691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1701778691" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1701778691?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=2016-re-reads">2016-re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1701778691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5411431266519435149"><b>SPOILERS WHICH I WONT MARK SORRY AND REALLY CRAP REVIEW BECAUSE I JUST DONT CARE</b><br/><br/><i>Boundless</i> was a book I chose to read to get it out of my TBR. Ultimately, it was a re-read of a series once loved and treasured by myself. Now, it's a book I found myself cringing at the idea of even recognising I read - my sincere apologies to the author considering I once did <b>adore</b> these characters and stories. <br/><br/>It's possible I'm falling into a slump though considering my average rating lately has been a 3. If I do </span>
  <span id="freeText5411431266519435149" style="display:none"><b>SPOILERS WHICH I WONT MARK SORRY AND REALLY CRAP REVIEW BECAUSE I JUST DONT CARE</b><br /><br /><i>Boundless</i> was a book I chose to read to get it out of my TBR. Ultimately, it was a re-read of a series once loved and treasured by myself. Now, it's a book I found myself cringing at the idea of even recognising I read - my sincere apologies to the author considering I once did <b>adore</b> these characters and stories. <br /><br />It's possible I'm falling into a slump though considering my average rating lately has been a 3. If I do fall into the horrific slump I'm blaming <i>The Darkest Minds</i> <br /><br />I skimmed this book though to be honest. I didn't enjoy it so I didn't want to read it like I would another book, so I don't remember a whole lot from it. <br /><br />Before we start, some quotes: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“What’s the matter, kid?” she asks when I don’t answer. “Vision got you down?”<br /><br />I gulp in a breath. “How did you know?”<br /><br />“I get them, too. Plus I’ve been hanging around people who have visions for most of my life. I recognize the post-vision face.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Okay, just the one. I thought that one was amusing and gave me flashbacks to That's So Raven. Most of the quotes in this book were eye roll worthy, though this is probably the best book in the series and I'm endlessly proud of Clara for not buying into the soul mate crap with Christian. <br /><br /><i>Characters</i><br /><br /><b>Clara</b> had some great character development. I still hated her, but I found her absolutely infuriating still. She made some dumb decisions and her whole entire mind tended to focus on irrelevant things e.g. boys and her crappy friend Angela (I have a lot of feelings about her which I won't include in this review.)<br /><br /><b>Tucker</b> has been the most sane person in this whole trilogy. His actions make sense and I wouldn't have been mad if he hadn't have gotten back with Clara because I love him. <br /><br /><b>Christian</b> may have been better in this book but doesn't mean I didn't want to punch him in the nose like eighty times throughout this book. I mean, he definitely deserved the nose jab too - it would be worth the broken hand. <br /><br />I don't even want to talk about the world building, plot or writing. I just want to put this series behind me. I'm glad I'm done. I'm upset I didn't connect with these characters as much. I would recommend this series to a younger audience perhaps, but possibly not to an older one. Maybe it's just me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5411431266519435149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_485734545" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485734545" />
    <a title="Mitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch"><img alt="Mitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208595p2/8170554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/485734545?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitch" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch">Mitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer485734545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15406314608490102197">Sorry, I tried, but I just don’t get the appeal. I’ve heard lots of good things ever since <i>Unearthly</i> and I certainly understand the praise - in an angel paranormal landscape littered with train wrecks like <i>Silence</i>, <i>Halo</i>, and <i>Hush, Hush</i>, <i>Boundless</i> is far from terrible. Still, when I’m looking at the story, all I see are the same generic concepts as pretty much every other book in the genre, just better done. That’s great for people who actually enjoy reading about romantic woes, love triangles, a</span>
  <span id="freeText15406314608490102197" style="display:none">Sorry, I tried, but I just don’t get the appeal. I’ve heard lots of good things ever since <i>Unearthly</i> and I certainly understand the praise - in an angel paranormal landscape littered with train wrecks like <i>Silence</i>, <i>Halo</i>, and <i>Hush, Hush</i>, <i>Boundless</i> is far from terrible. Still, when I’m looking at the story, all I see are the same generic concepts as pretty much every other book in the genre, just better done. That’s great for people who actually enjoy reading about romantic woes, love triangles, and a smidge of plotting just so we can say there’s a story beyond just the romance, but I don’t think I can ever get beyond the fact that this is still really just a romance masquerading as an angel plot.<br /><br />And ultimately, that's my problem. Say what you will about how great <i>Boundless</i> is, but, at the end of the day, it still has more in common with its oft ridiculed peers than with a true angel book. Sure, the girl is a little less angsty and not quite so insecure, the love triangle isn't nauseatingly vomitrocious, and the plot is a bit more than just your average good versus evil angels capped off by your typical fight to stave off the end of the world as we know it, but in the end <i>Boundless</i> is still working with the same ingredients that made all those other angel books 'bad' - can I really say this is 'good' when it's the book equivalent of making the same shitty stew but using slightly better quality ingredients? Why does Clara have to spend fully half the book doing random college stuff with Christian while her father conveniently withholds the vital stuff that moves the plot along in the second half until the midway point of the book? Why does she spend so much time obsessing over her failed relationship with Tucker to the point the actual plot involving the threat to her life feels more like a minor inconvenience? Why does the climax of this book fail as much as <i>Unearthly</i> - when Clara basically just ripped off some dude's ear? If I can make a comparison to <i>Heaven</i>, another angel book with a superficially similar plot, yeah, at least Hand's protagonist isn't shallow or sanctimonious and her depictions of college life aren’t nearly as laughable, but when all’s said and done I don’t think there’s really anything here I haven’t seen before there.<br /><br />Actually, maybe there is one thing, something that's bothered me ever since <i>Unearthly</i> - Hand's excessive use of foreshadowing. Part of it, Clara's vision starting out the prologue and the rest of the book being her trying to figure out her purpose and the end revealing how her initial vision worked out, well, that I get is the hook of the series and have no problems with, but it seems to me like Hand enjoys revealing things with basically the writing equivalent of 'see, see, here's a detail that's going to be important later, so I'm going to make it so obvious you HAVE to notice it' - there was the color of Jeffrey's wings the last two books, and this time around, all the stuff about how something is going on with Angela. But you know what? After all the foreshadowing, you don't just reveal exactly what I've been expecting based on all the hints marked by the big neon signs, otherwise the reveal just becomes anticlimatical, and anticlimatical reveals are boring. My reaction before reading this book was seriously 'you can't muck up the last book in the series with excessive foreshadowing, can you?' - and somehow, I was still bored, because Hand really doesn't deliver with the 'is Jeffrey good or evil because of the color of his wings' plot she's got going on for two books now, THAT was textbook anticlimatical, and Angela's storyline really wasn't any better. I don't think I learned anything about how her relationship with Phen <s>evolves</s> devolves after what happened.<br /><br />The worst thing by far though, is the love triangle. I'm sure that's a bonus for lots of people, but for me, it's a massive detriment. Why? I don't get the appeal of Tucker. He's just a cowboy who can't do anything because everyone else has angel powers, so Clara's relationship with him is basically 'she's out saving the world while he's back at the ranch doing... manly things?' - so I see all my friends rooting for Tucker and I'm like, 'umm why?' because he comes dangerously close through most of the book of falling into the useless love interest trap, and I have no patience with useless characters. Then again, even though Christian does things, I don't like him either, but at least there I'm not alone. For me, the only thing the triangle does is give a license for all these characters to act like jerks whenever it's brought it, and why is that a good thing? And the other thing about love triangles is that you have to write the ending a certain way, otherwise you piss off your fanbase, so while I think many many people will be very happy after reading the ending - even if many others will be disappointed, it doesn't really make much sense. Not spoiling it, but the whole point of Clara's triangle dilemma is left unresolved except for a massive <i>deus ex machina</i> delivered by Uriel. <br /><br />Yeah, basically, I'm thankful this series is over because I'm not the kind of guy who enjoys reading about people bitching about their love lives for most of a book that's nominally supposed to be about conflict between Heaven and Hell. A conflict that's not even well done thanks to all the huge hints scattered throughout that left me five steps ahead of Clara and company the entire time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15406314608490102197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6990738678141706159">I liked that this was set in college. I liked the emphasis on choosing your own destiny. I liked how it showed the healing power of love (not just romantic love). I like these characters and was really invested in them throughout the series. I also just plain liked the angels and angelbloods.<br/><br/>What I didn't really like was how small the battle ended up being. I mean, it's a huge deal for the main character because it's about the people she loves, but I thought this was gearing up for something big</span>
  <span id="freeText6990738678141706159" style="display:none">I liked that this was set in college. I liked the emphasis on choosing your own destiny. I liked how it showed the healing power of love (not just romantic love). I like these characters and was really invested in them throughout the series. I also just plain liked the angels and angelbloods.<br /><br />What I didn't really like was how small the battle ended up being. I mean, it's a huge deal for the main character because it's about the people she loves, but I thought this was gearing up for something bigger. Although, I have to be honest, most trilogies that I've read that do try to take on something HUGE fail spectacularly. So maybe it was for the best?<br /><br />Anyway - not a fave and not without flaws, but I did enjoy this series! I binge read all 3 books in just a few days. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer245059285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14301135655100528130"><b>My initial thoughts after finishing:</b><br/><br/>There were moments like this:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364629ra/716386.gif' alt='image' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>and this:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/670000.gif' height='282' width='500' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>but ultimately, I feel like this:<br/><br/><img alt='satisfied' height='176' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364629ra/716387.gif' width='320' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It's over, and I'm sad about that, but I'm satisfied. <br/><br/>--------------------------------<br/><br/><b>Full review:</b><br/><br/>Fair warning:  I'm probably going to ramble -- <i>without spoilers</i> -- in this review and it might get painfully awkward at times.  My apologies in advance.  But when one of your favorite series comes to an end, a fair amount of gushing and tears is expected...deserved, even.  Yes, I'm sad to say g</span>
  <span id="freeText14301135655100528130" style="display:none"><b>My initial thoughts after finishing:</b><br><br>There were moments like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364629ra/716386.gif" alt="image" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/670000.gif" height="282" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>but ultimately, I feel like this:<br><br><img alt="satisfied" height="176" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364629ra/716387.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's over, and I'm sad about that, but I'm satisfied. <br><br>--------------------------------<br><br><b>Full review:</b><br><br>Fair warning:  I'm probably going to ramble -- <i>without spoilers</i> -- in this review and it might get painfully awkward at times.  My apologies in advance.  But when one of your favorite series comes to an end, a fair amount of gushing and tears is expected...deserved, even.  Yes, I'm sad to say goodbye to these characters, but I'm also happy to have met them.<br><br>The first thing that always strikes me when I pick up a Cynthia Hand novel is how genuine, how authentic they feel.  Clara's voice is sincere and realistic...she sounds like a real teenager -- not the facade that television or society might think of as one, but an actual teenager.   Clara is tenacious and snarky and completely relatable...aside from that whole angel-blood thing.  The dialogue in these books is superbly done, as if I'm having a conversation with old friends, not just reading about it.  And Clara's interactions with other characters are as unpretentious as always, even when she's dealing with a Black Wing.  If there's one character I wish were real, it's Clara...I'd make her my best friend in a heartbeat.  I've always assumed that Clara was a reflection of the author, so in that case, <i>Can we be best friends, Cynthia</i>?  :0)<br><br>
  <img alt="" height="200" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/438508.gif" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>Something else to take note of in Hand's novels is the importance of family.  Sure, Clara and Jeffrey's father wasn't around much during the formidable teenage years, but not by choice, and they had the most awesome, caring mother to make up for it.  Maggie is the mother of all YA mothers, and she proves that there doesn't have to be a lack of parental figures in a young adult's life for them to find their share of trouble.  Even Clara's wayward brother Jeffrey plays an important role in this series...he's not just a barely there side character.  In fact, none of the secondary cast of characters is a bit player.  They all have a significant role in how the bigger picture unfolds.<br><br>And what a big, beautiful picture this series has turned out to be!  So many things I never saw coming!  More visions.  More danger.  More everything.  The pacing starts off nice and slow, with Clara embarking on her first year of college at Stanford, but for an angel-blood having visions of doom and gloom, life is never easy.  Clara soon begins to wonder if she's been deluding herself into believing that she might be able to lead a normal life.  But just as Clara has discovered with her purpose, things happen for a reason, whether you believe in fate or not.  There were some truly pivotal moments in this final book, some that I can't yet comment upon, but this story is such a thing of beauty.<br><br>So much transpires in this novel, so many secrets and hidden truths uncovered, and yet, just as I was figuring things out for myself, so were the characters.  I didn't have to wait 100 pages for them to catch on, which is really refreshing.  Just goes to show how truly genuine the characters and story are...we're always on the same page.<br><br>Even with Clara's decision to distance herself from Tucker in order to protect him.  I usually hate when a fictional guy does this to a girl.  But in Clara's case, we already know the danger; we know it's not a gimmick.  The Black Wings are a real threat.  Doesn't make it hurt less, though.  At the end of <i>Hallowed</i>, I couldn't have told you if Clara would end up with Tucker or Christian...and I couldn't have made that decision myself, if I'd been in her shoes.  Both were equally good <i>to</i> her and <i>for</i> her, in their own ways.  In <i>Boundless</i>, that isn't any less true.  Both think that they are each meant to be with Clara.  She's definitely got a difficult road and some tough choices ahead of her.<br><br>Lots of changes in <i>Boundless</i>.  Lots of appearances from old friends.  It's a lot to take in.  But it's a satisfying ending to a breath-taking series that I won't soon forget.  I can't imagine having never met these characters or sharing in their experiences as they came to terms with who and what they were.  Full of humor, love, and possibility, this brilliant series is not to be missed.  I can't wait to see what else Cynthia Hand has up her sleeve!<br><br>Also, don't forget to stop by <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starry-Eyed Revue</a> on the 24th for a Q &amp; A with the author -- in which she divulges what type of reader <i>she</i> is -- as part of the <a href="http://mundiemomsblogtours.blogspot.com/2013/01/blog-tour-boundless-unearthly-3-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Boundless Blog Tour</a> hosted by Mundie Moms!<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-OtYw4PbfHvQ/UPStLowKjYI/AAAAAAAAK8Y/6Af_R9ZooYU/s1600/Boundlessbanner.JPG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="133" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364629i/716388.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Thanks to HarperTeen for providing an ARC for review!</i><br><br>This review can also be found at <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/01/review-boundless-by-cynthia-hand.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14301135655100528130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText12874614511135331602" style="display:none">Hey, would you like at that. I'm actually posting something for a book that didn't come out yet. A book I haven't read, but I know I'm going to freakin' love anyway. As long as Clara and Tucker get back together, that is. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380369100i/721792.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Look Clara, screw Christian. (Not literally, please.) Remember that jaw-dropping hot guy named Tucker? You know, the one you <i>Have. To. Love?</i> If you don't, I'll smack you until it all comes back. <br><br><b>Edited: 6/21/12</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/488303.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>IT HAS A COVER!</b> And one that isn't a complete change of what we had going on for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a> too! I have to say, I'm impressed. The constant changes in YA covers, and with YA in general, has not been impressing me lately. //<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zQJj6dUjn4c9Nm8DAT+EgvSucXSVUB9l/PVZ1nMjK5w18puH3K0+DuXPFK/0SUoz/Ntkb5vUlEtsWL5lEXCyOQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t9EOQH/o/j2j0xCordnL8uAfUzmnJtnF5Unvm8clNwJPIfYudmZftHsqawRYrwVD6GpGIqmiUut15AgopXaupw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer17645214065831987598">Cynthia Hand is the New York Times bestselling author of several books for teens, including the UNEARTHLY trilogy, THE LAST TIME WE SAY GOODBYE, MY LADY JANE and MY PLAIN JANE (with fellow authors Brodi Ashton and Jodi Meadows), THE AFTERLIFE OF HOLLY CHASE, and the upcoming novels THE HOW AND THE WHY and MY CALAMITY JANE (also with Ashton and Meadows). Before turning to writing for young adults, </span>
  <span id="freeText17645214065831987598" style="display:none">Cynthia Hand is the New York Times bestselling author of several books for teens, including the UNEARTHLY trilogy, THE LAST TIME WE SAY GOODBYE, MY LADY JANE and MY PLAIN JANE (with fellow authors Brodi Ashton and Jodi Meadows), THE AFTERLIFE OF HOLLY CHASE, and the upcoming novels THE HOW AND THE WHY and MY CALAMITY JANE (also with Ashton and Meadows). Before turning to writing for young adults, she studied literary fiction and earned both an M.F.A. and a Ph.D. in fiction writing. She currently resides in Boise, Idaho, with her husband, two cats, one crazy dog, two kids, and mountain of books.</span>
